كتاب احياء الموات
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر کنواں پانی پلانے کے لئے ہو تو اس کا حریم چالیس ذراع ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے جس نے کنواں کھودا تو اس کے لئے اس کے ارد گرد چالیس ذراع میں اپنے چوپاؤں کو بٹھانے کے لئے پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ ہر جانب سے چالیس ہیں ( یعنی مجموعی چالیس) اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ چالیس ہر جانب سے ہیں اس لئے کہ زمینوں میں نرمی ہے اور لوٹ جائے گا پانی اس کنویں کی جانب جو اس سے کم میں کھودا جائے گا اور اگر کنوں سچائی کے لیے ہو تو اس کا حریم ساٹھ ذراع ہے اور یہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک چالیس ذراع ہے ۔
تشریح ماقبل میں یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی تھی کہ کنویں کے لئے حریم ہو گا اب سوال پیدا ہوا کہ حریم کتنا ہوگا تو فرمایا کہ اگر کنواں اس لئے ہو کہ اس سے ہاتھ سے پانی کھینچ کر جانوروں کو پلایا جائے گا اور اسکے پاس جانور آرام کرلیں تو ایسے کنویں کا حریم چالیس ذراع ہے یعنی ہر طرف سے چالیس چالیس ذراع اور اگر کنواں اس لئے ہو کہ اس سے کھیتوں کو سیراب کیا جائے گا تو اس کے حریم میں اختلاف ہے امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس کا حریم بھی چالیس ذراع ہے۔
اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کا حریم سامچھ ذراع ہے فریقین کے دلائل آگے مذکور ہیں۔ بیر عطن کا حریم چالیس ذراع ہے اسکے بارے میں حدیث مذکور ہے۔ یہ حدیث ابن ماجہ اور مسند احمد میں ہے اول بروایت عبد اللہ بن مغفل اور ثانی بروایت ابو ہریرہ۔
تنبیه
عطن۔ کنویں کے اردگر دادونوں کو بٹھانے کی جگہ اور بیر بطن سے مراد وہ کنواں جس کا مقصد صرف جانوروں کو پانی پلاتا ہو کھیتوں کی سیرابی اس کا مقصد نہ ہو۔
ناضح ، حقیقت میں اس اونٹ کو کہتے ہیں جو عطن میں چھٹر کا ؤکر دے پھر ہر اونٹ کے اندر اسکا استعمال ہونے لگا اگر چہ وہ اپنے او پر پانی نہ لادے، اور چرس اور رہٹ میں چونکہ اونٹ یا بیل جوڑ کر کام لیا جاتا تھا کچھ دنوں پہلے تک اس کا رواج تھا آجکل تو ہمارے علاقہ میں اس کا رواج ختم ہو گیا اور بجلی کی ٹیوبل نے اس کی جگہ لے لی ) اس لئے ایسے کنویں کو بیر ناضح کہا گیا ہے تو بیر ناضح سے مراد وہ کنواں جس سے کھیتوں کو سینچا جائے۔ تنبیہ چالیس ذراع ہو ہر جانب سے معتبر ہے ہو اصحیح سکب الا نبرص ۴۹۱ ج ۲
،
تنبیہ ۳ رہٹ وغیرہ میں امام صاحب اور صاحبین کا اختلاف مذکور ہوا۔ فتاویٰ تا تارخانیہ اور فتاوی کبری میں صاحبین کے قول کو مفتی بہ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ درمختار میں امام صاحب کے قول کو مفتی بہ قرار دیا گیا ہے علامہ قاسم ابن قطلو بنانے قول امام کو ترجیح دی ہے صاحب ہدایہ کا اسلوب بھی ترجیح قول امام و مقتضی ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل
لهما قوله عليه السلام حريم العين خمسمائة ذراع وحريم بير العطن اربعون ذراعا وحريم بير الناضح ستون ذراعا ولانه قد يحتاج فيه الى ان يسير دابته للاستقاء وقد يطول الرشاء وبير العطن للاستفاع منه
The extent of the harim of a well for watering animals (birr 'atan): statements of jurists. He said: If it is for watering animals, then its harim is forty cubits, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever digs a well, for him is what is around it, forty cubits, as a resting place for his cattle.' Then it was said forty cubits from each side, and the correct is from each side because the lands are soft and water will transfer to what is dug beyond it. And if it is for irrigation (nadih), then its harim is sixty cubits; this is according to them (the two companions), and according to Abu Hanifa it is forty cubits. Translation (from al-Quduri): So if the well is for watering animals, its harim is forty cubits, due to the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Whoever digs a well, for him is around it forty cubits for resting his cattle.' Then it was said forty from all sides, and the correct is that it is from all sides, because the lands are soft, and water will revert to the well that is dug beyond it. And if the well is for irrigation, its harim is sixty cubits; this is according to the two companions, and according to Abu Hanifa it is forty cubits. Explanation: In the previous section, it became known that there is a harim for the well. Now the question arose: how much is the harim? He said: If the well is such that water is drawn by hand to water animals and they rest near it, then its harim is forty cubits from each side. And if the well is for irrigating fields, then there is a dispute: according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), its harim is also forty cubits; according to the two companions, its harim is sixty cubits. The proofs of both parties are mentioned below. The harim of a well for animals (birr 'atan) is forty cubits, and a hadith is mentioned about it. This hadith is in Ibn Majah and Musnad Ahmad, first from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal and second from Abu Huraira. Note: 'Atan' is the place around the well where cattle are made to rest. Birr 'atan means the well whose purpose is only to water animals, not to irrigate fields. 'Nadih' originally refers to the camel that draws water from the well, then it came to be used for any such well, even if the animal does not carry water. Since in the past, oxen or camels were used for drawing water from wells for irrigation, such a well is called birr nadih. So birr nadih means the well from which fields are irrigated. Note: The correct view is that the forty cubits are from each side (Sukb al-Inbaras, vol. 2, p. 491). Note 3: The difference between Imam and the two companions regarding wells with waterwheels etc. has been mentioned. In Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya and Fatawa Kubra, the statement of the two companions is considered mufta bihi. In Durr Mukhtar, the statement of Imam is considered mufta bihi. Allamah Qasim Ibn Qatlu Bana preferred Imam's statement. The style of the author of Hidayah also indicates preference for Imam's statement. The proof of the two companions: For them is his statement, peace be upon him: 'The harim of a spring is five hundred cubits, the harim of a well for animals is forty cubits, and the harim of a well for irrigation is sixty cubits.' And because it may need for his animal to walk for drawing water, and the rope may be long; while the well for animals is for immediate use from it.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents the detailed rulings on the precise dimensions of the harim (protected perimeter) for different types of wells. The text first distinguishes between two kinds of wells: birr 'atan (for watering animals) and birr nadih (for irrigation). For the former, all agree on 40 cubits from each side, based on the hadith. For the latter, Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is also 40 cubits, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is 60 cubits. The commentary explains the reasoning: for irrigation wells, the animal drawing water may need to walk, and the rope may be longer, hence a larger harim is needed. The passage also notes the hadith evidence from Ibn Majah and Musnad Ahmad. Finally, it cites later fatwa works that weigh the two views: some prefer the Sahibayn, others prefer Imam Abu Hanifa, indicating that the matter has considerable authority on both sides.

Key Terms
عطن ('atan): The area around a well where cattle are made to rest while being watered.
ناضح (nadih): A well used for irrigation; originally referred to the animal that draws water.
حریم (harim): The protected perimeter around a well, measured in cubits, within which no other well or building is allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the harim of a well used for irrigation (birr nadih)?
A) 40 cubits
B) 60 cubits
C) 500 cubits
D) 100 cubits

Key Takeaway
The harim of an irrigation well is disputed within the Hanafi school: 40 cubits (Abu Hanifa) or 60 cubits (Sahibayn), and later authorities differ on which view is mufta bihi.

10 min
The Harim of Wells: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the extent of harim for different well types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the harim of different wells, and explain the proofs each side uses, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: 40 cubits for all wells. Sahibayn: 40 for hand-drawn, 60 for animal-drawn wells.

The harim (protected area) around a well prevents mutual damage. But how much area should be protected? Within the Hanafi school, there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). This lesson unpacks their proofs and the practical difference this makes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: a uniform harim of 40 cubits for all wells, regardless of type.
This is based on a general hadith and qiyas.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the position of the Sahibayn: they differentiate between wells of 'aṭan (40 cubits) and nāḍiḥ (60 cubits).
Their evidence includes a mursal hadith and rational need.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Sahibayn's main arguments: the mursal hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and the rational need for larger harim in nāḍiḥ wells due to longer ropes and animal movement.
The reliability of the mursal hadith is noted.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Study Abu Hanifa's counterarguments: his general hadith is agreed upon and acted upon, while the specific hadith is disputed. Qiyas is abandoned where hadiths agree (40 cubits) and preserved where they conflict (60 cubits). Also, need can be equalized by using a pulley.
This shows the application of usul principles: preferring the general over the specific when there is dispute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: the Sahibayn's view gives a larger protected area (60 cubits) for irrigation wells, while Abu Hanifa gives 40 for all. Later Hanafi fatwa often prefers the Sahibayn's differentiation.
This affects how close a new well can be dug near an existing one.

كتاب احياء الموات
ترجمہ صاحبین کی دلیل نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے، کہ چشمہ کا حریم پانچسو ذراع اور بیر عطن کا حریم چالیس ذراع ہے اور بیر ناضح کا حریم ساٹھ ذراع ہے اور اس لئے کہ کبھی اس میں سیرابی کے لئے چوپایہ کو چلانے کی حاجت پیش آتی ہے اور کبھی رہی لمبی ہو جاتی ہے اور پیر عطن پانی کھینچنے کے لئے ہے اپنے ہاتھ سے تو حاجت کم ہوگی تو تفاوت ضروری ہے۔
تشریح حضرات صاحبین نے اختلافی مسئلہ میں اپنے قول پر یہ دلیل پیش فرمائی ہے اولاً حدیث جو سعید بن مسیب کی مرسل ہے جس کو مند کہنا وہم ہے لیکن مُرسل بھی بایں الفاظ نہیں ہے دوسری دلیل عقلی کہ بیر ناضح میں چڑسوں میں اونٹ وغیرہ جوڑے جاتے ہیں اور بسا اوقات رسا (بیٹر ) لمبا ہو جاتا ہے تو اس میں زیادہ حریم کی ضرورت ہے لہذا ساٹھ قرار دیا گیا ہے اور بیر عطن میں اس کی حاجت نہیں کیونکہ اس میں سے پانی ہاتھ سے کھینچا جاتا ہے۔ لہذا ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق کرنا ضروری ہے کہ اول میں چالیس اور ثانی میں ساتھ ذراع ہوں۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله ما رويناه من غير فصل و العام المتفق على قبوله والعمل به اولى عنده من الخاص المختلف في قبوله والعمل به و لان القياس یابی استحقاق الحريم لان عمله في موضع الحفر والاستحقاق به ففيما اتفق عليه الحديثان تركناه وفيما تعارضافيه حفظناه ولانه قد يستقى من العطن بالناضح ومن بير الناضح باليد فاستوت الحاجة فيهما ويمكنه ان يدير البعير حول البير فلا يحتاج الى زيادة مسافة اقتباس اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں بغیر تفصیل کے اور وہ عام جس کے قبول کرنے پر اور اس پر عمل کرنے پر اتفاق ہو اولی ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس خاص سے جس کی قبولیت اور اس پر عمل کئے جانے میں اختلاف ہو اور اس لئے کہ قیاس حریم کے استحقاق سے منع کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ حاضر کا عمل کھودنے کی جگہ میں ہے اور استحقاق عمل کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے تو جس مقدار یعے نوں حدیثیں متفق ہو گئی ہیں ہم نے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا اور جس مقدار میں متعارض ہیں ہم نے قیاس کو ملحوظ رکھا، اور اس لئے کہ کبھی بیر عطن سے اونٹ کے ذریعہ پانی نکالا جاتا ہے اور بیر ناضح سے ہاتھ سے نکالا جاتا ہے تو دونوں میں حاجت برابر رہی اور ممکن ہے اس کو یہ کہ اونٹ کو کنویں کے ارد گرد گھو مائے تو زیادہ مسافت کی حاجت نہ ہوگی۔
تشریح یہ حضرت امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہماری روایت کردہ پہلی حدیث مـن حـفــر بـيـر .... الخ - يد حدیث عام ہر کنویں کو بیر عطن ہو یا بیر ناضح پھر اسی مقدار تک سب کا اتفاق ہے اور اس مقدار پر سب کا عمل ہے اور صاحبین کی ذکر کردہ حدیث وہ خاص ہے کیونکہ اس میں بیر عطن اور بیر ناضح کا حکم الگ الگ بیان کیا گیا ہے، پھر اس کے قبول کرنے میں اور اس پر عمل کرنے میں اختلاف بھی ہے تو خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ حدیث اول عام ہے متفق علیہ ہے معمول یہ ہے اور دوسری خاص ہے۔ مختلف فیہ ہے تو ایسی صورت میں امام صاحب کے اصول کے مطابق اول قابل ترجیح ہوگی۔ دوسری دلیل ... قیاس یہ چاہتا ہے کہ حریم بالکل نہ ملے کیونکہ استحقاق عمل کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اور کھودنے والے کا عمل کھودنے کی جگہ تک ہے تو حریم نہ ملنا چاہیے۔ تو ہم نے کہا کہ جس مقدار پر دو حدیثیں متفق ہیں وہاں ہم قیاس کو چھوڑ دیں گے اور جہاں مختلف ہیں وہاں ہم قیاس سے کام لیں گے اور چالیس میں متفق اور ساتھ میں مختلف ہیں تو ہم نے چالیس کو لے لیا ہے۔ تیسری دلیل ... بیر عطن سے کبھی اونٹ کے ذریعہ پانی نکالا جاتا ہے اور کبھی بیر ناضح سے ہاتھ سے پانی نکالا جاتا ہے تو ضرورت دونوں میں برابر ہی لہذ امقدار بھی برابر ہوگی یعنی چالیس ذراع ۔ چوتھی دلیل آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کبھی رشا در از ہو جاتا ہے تو زیادہ جگہ کی حاجت پڑتی ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ ضرورت تو چڑسوں میں پڑے گی رہٹ میں نہیں پڑے گی لہذا اس کو چاہیے کہ رہنٹ سے کام لے۔
تنبیہ پہلی صورت کو عام کہنا محل تأمل ہے کیونکہ اس میں عطن لماشستہ کی قید موجود ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ بیر عطن کا حکم ہے؟
جواب ..... من حفر بيرا عام ہے ہر کنویں کو اس میں کچھ قید نہیں ہے تو یہ دونوں کنوؤں کو شامل ہے اور فـلـه مـمـا حولها اربعون ذراعاً ۔ اسی مطلق بیئر کی جزاء اور حکم ہے اور پھر بعد میں عطن لما شیته فرمانا تقید نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ غالب احوال پر محمول کرتے ہوئے حریم بیر کی منفعت کا ذکر ہے او بیر عطن اور بیر ناضح کے ارد گرد اونٹ وغیرہ بٹھا دیئے جاتے ہیں بالفاظ دیگر یہ تغلیب پر محمول ہے نہ کہ تقیید پر جیسے وذر والبیع میں بھی تغلیب کا لحاظ ہے نہ کہ تقیید کا۔
تنبیه - ۲ مصنف نے ولانه قدیستگی ... الخ ۔ سے جو تعلیل بیان فرمائی ہے علیل ہے اور تصریحات سابقہ کے خلاف ہے نیز اگر ایسا ہو جائے تو اس سے بیر عطن یا بیر ناضح کی حقیقت متغیر نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of Reviving Dead Lands. Translation: The Sahibayn's proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The harim of a spring is five hundred cubits, the harim of a well of 'atan is forty cubits, and the harim of a well of nadih is sixty cubits.' And because sometimes there is a need to drive livestock for watering, and sometimes the rope becomes long, and the well of 'atan is for drawing water by hand, so the need is less, hence differentiation is necessary. Elaboration: The honorable Sahibayn presented this proof in the disputed matter: first, a hadith narrated by Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab as mursal (calling it munkar is a delusion, but even the mursal is not in these words). Second, a rational proof: in a nadih well, camels etc. are yoked to a wheel, and sometimes the rope becomes long, so a larger harim is needed, hence sixty is set; for a well of 'atan, because water is drawn by hand, the need is less, so differentiating between them is necessary: the former has forty and the latter sixty cubits. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof: 'And his proof is what we have narrated without distinction, and the general (hadith) whose acceptance and practice are agreed upon is preferable to him over the specific (hadith) whose acceptance and practice are disputed. And because analogy (qiyas) prevents entitlement to harim, since his work is at the digging site and entitlement is by work. So in what the two hadiths agree upon, we leave analogy; and in what they contradict, we preserve it. And because sometimes water is drawn from a well of 'atan by a nadih, and from a well of nadih by hand, so the need is equal in both, and (the owner) can make the camel go around the well, so he does not need extra distance.' Translation: And Abu Hanifah's proof is the hadith we have narrated without distinction, and the general (hadith) whose acceptance and practice are agreed upon is preferable to him over the specific (hadith) whose acceptance and practice are disputed. And because analogy prevents entitlement to harim, since the worker's work is at the digging site and entitlement is by work. So in the amount where the two hadiths agree, we leave analogy; and where they contradict, we consider analogy. And because sometimes from a well of 'atan water is drawn by camel, and from a well of nadih by hand, so the need is equal in both, and it is possible for him to circle the camel around the well, so he will not need extra distance. Elaboration: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifah. Its summary is that the first hadith we narrated ('Whoever digs a well...') is a general hadith covering every well, whether 'aṭan or nāḍiḥ. Then everyone agrees on that amount and acts upon it. The hadith mentioned by the Ṣāḥibayn is specific because it gives separate rulings for 'aṭan and nāḍiḥ. Moreover, there is dispute over its acceptance and practice. So the conclusion is that the first hadith is general, agreed upon, and acted upon; the second is specific and disputed. In such a case, according to Imam's principle, the first deserves preference. Second proof: Analogy requires that no harim be given at all, because entitlement is proven by work, and the digger's work is only at the digging site, so no harim should be given. We say: in the amount where the two hadiths agree, we leave analogy; where they differ, we use analogy. They agree on forty and differ on sixty, so we adopt forty. Third proof: Sometimes water is drawn from a well of 'atan by camel and from a well of nadih by hand, so the need in both is equal, hence the amount should also be equal: forty cubits. Fourth proof: The opponent says sometimes the rope becomes long, so extra space is needed. The answer is that this need arises only with the 'churras' (wheel) not with the 'rahaṭ' (pulley), so one should use the rahaṭ. Warning 1: Calling the first form 'general' is questionable because it contains the restriction 'aṭan lima sḥtah' (a well of 'atan for what one desires), meaning it is the ruling for a well of 'atan. Answer: 'Whoever digs a well' is general, covering every well; it has no restriction. So it includes both wells, and 'for him from around it forty cubits' is the ruling for the absolute 'birr'. Then saying 'aṭan lima sḥtah' afterwards is not a restriction, but rather it is interpreted according to dominant circumstances: it mentions the benefit of the harim, and camels etc. are seated around the well of 'aṭan and nāḍiḥ. In other words, it is interpreted as taghlīb (predominance) not taqyīd (restriction), just as in 'wadharr wa al-bay' (the hadith of harm and sale) taghlīb is considered, not taqyīd. Warning 2: The author's explanation from 'li-annahu qad yastuqī...' is weak and contradicts previous statements. Also, even if such a situation occurs, it does not change the reality of a well of 'aṭan or nāḍiḥ.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the extent of the harim (protected area) around wells. The Sahibayn differentiate between a well of 'aṭan (used for drawing water by hand) and a well of nāḍiḥ (used for irrigation with animals), assigning a harim of 40 cubits to the former and 60 cubits to the latter. Their evidence includes a mursal hadith attributed to Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and a rational argument that the greater need in a nāḍiḥ well (because of longer ropes and animal movement) requires a larger harim. Imam Abu Hanifah, however, holds a uniform harim of 40 cubits for all wells. His reasoning is based on a general hadith (whoever digs a well has a harim of 40 cubits from around it), which he considers agreed upon and acted upon, whereas the Sahibayn's hadith is specific and disputed. He also uses analogy: since entitlement to harim is based on work at the digging site, no harim would be required by analogy, but he abandons analogy in the agreed-upon amount (40 cubits) and preserves it where the hadiths conflict (over 60). He further argues that the need for extra space can be met by using a pulley (rahaṭ) instead of a wheel, so differentiation is unnecessary. The commentary then provides two tanbihs (warnings). The first addresses a potential criticism: the first hadith might be considered specific because it mentions 'aṭan. The response is that 'min ḥafara bi'ran' is general, and the mention of 'aṭan is not a restriction but a predominant usage. The second tanbih criticizes the author's own reasoning in the text, pointing out its weakness and inconsistency with earlier statements.

Key Terms
حریم (ḥarīm): The protected area around a well or spring where digging another well is prohibited to prevent mutual damage.
بیر عطن (bi'r 'aṭan): A well where water is drawn by hand using a rope and bucket; usually for domestic use.
بیر ناضح (bi'r nāḍiḥ): A well where water is drawn using an animal-driven wheel; used for irrigation.
ذراع (dhirā'): A unit of length, approximately one cubit (elbow to fingertip).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the harim of a well of 'aṭan?
A) 40 cubits
B) 60 cubits
C) 500 cubits
D) No harim

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa holds a uniform 40-cubit harim for all wells, while the Sahibayn differentiate based on the well's function, a disagreement rooted in different interpretations of hadith and qiyas.

Ruling on the Harim of a Spring
States the ruling for the harim of a spring as 500 cubits on each side.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the harim of a spring in Hanafi law and explain the reasoning behind the measurement.

Core Idea
A spring's harim is 500 cubits on each side because of divine revelation and practical need.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the protected area around a spring. Al-Quduri states that the harim is 500 cubits, based on both a narrated hadith and practical agricultural needs. We will explore the proof, the measurement method, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? What is the ruling (wajib, haram, etc.) regarding the harim of a spring?
The harim is a protected strip of land; it is obligatory to observe it.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? There is a hadith (narrated earlier) and a rational argument based on need.
The hadith gives the number; the need justifies the larger size compared to a well.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the hadith prove the ruling? It specifies 500 cubits for a spring. The rational argument shows why more space is needed.
The spring is dug for agriculture, requiring channels and basins.
4
Note the measurement and variations
What is the most correct (al-ashah) measurement? It is 500 cubits from each side, not total. Also note the type of cubit (kasrawi) and the exception for soft lands.
The cubit used is the broken cubit; in soft lands the distance may increase.
5
Understand the underlying principle
Why is the harim determined partly by revelation (tawqif) and partly by need? This shows the interplay of naql and aql in Hanafi fiqh.
The specific number is from revelation; the concept of protecting water sources is rational.

He (al-Quduri) said: And if it is a spring, its harim is five hundred cubits, due to what we have narrated, and because the need there is for extra distance. Since the spring is excavated for agriculture, there must be a place for water to flow, a basin to collect water, and a place for it to flow to the crops. Therefore, it is estimated with an increase, and the estimation of five hundred is by tawqīf (revelatory text). The most correct (opinion) is that it is five hundred cubits from every side, as we mentioned regarding the well of 'aṭan. And the cubit is the broken (kasrawī) cubit, which we have explained previously. And it has been said that the estimation for a spring and a well mentioned by us applies to their lands (soft lands) due to their hardness? Actually, in our lands (hard lands) it is increased so that water does not seep into the second (well) and spoil the first.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for the harim (protected area) of a spring. The author quotes al-Quduri's statement that the harim of a spring is 500 cubits. The proof is twofold: first, a hadith (which was narrated earlier in the text) that specifies this amount; second, rational reasoning: because springs are dug for agriculture, they require additional space for water channels, collection basins, and irrigation canals. Therefore, a larger harim is needed. The estimation of 500 cubits is from revelation (tawqīf). The most correct view (as explained in the text) is that the 500 cubits are measured from each side of the spring, similar to the well of 'aṭan (which had 40 cubits from each side). The cubit used is the 'kasrawī' cubit, a specific historical cubit. There is also a note that the estimation of 500 cubits for springs and 40/60 for wells applies to lands with hard soil; in soft soil, the distance might be increased to prevent water from seeping into neighboring properties and damaging the first excavation.

Key Terms
حریم (ḥarīm): The protected area around a spring or well where digging is prohibited to avoid damage.
عین ('ayn): A natural spring or man-dug water source for irrigation.
ذراع مکسرة (dhirā' mukassarah): The 'broken' or 'kasrawī' cubit, a specific measurement used in Hanafi law.
توقیف (tawqīf): Estimation by divine revelation (hadith), as opposed to qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 500 cubits from each side
C) 500 cubits from the front only
D) 40 cubits from each side

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the harim of a spring is 500 broken cubits on each side, based on a hadith and the need for agricultural irrigation.

The Harim of a Well: 40 Cubits and Its Proofs
Explanation of the ruling on well harim with four proofs and two tanbihat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the harim of a well and explain the proofs used to establish it, including the role of qiyas and resolving conflicting hadith texts.

Core Idea
The harim of every well is 40 cubits, established by hadith and qiyas, with exceptions resolved by pulley use.

The harim of a well is a protected area that must be left unobstructed. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the harim is 40 cubits from each side. The author presents four proofs: two hadiths, a qiyas between well types, and a response to an objection. We also learn how to harmonize conflicting narrations and the principle of leaving qiyas where the texts agree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi ruling: the harim of a well is 40 cubits from each side. Recognize that this is based on hadith and qiyas.
2
Understand the method of proof
Notice that the author uses agreement of two hadiths to leave qiyas, and difference to apply qiyas. This is a key usul principle.
The hadiths agree on 40 cubits for the 'atin well; their disagreement allows qiyas to extend to nadih.
3
Examine the qiyas
How does the author extend the ruling from 'atin well to nadih well? The illa (effective cause) is that both are wells used for drawing water, with equal need.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) based on common need.
4
Evaluate the objection and response
Some object that a nadih well may need more space due to a long rope. The response is that this only applies to bucket-drawn wells, so one should use a pulley instead.
This shows practical reasoning: if a need arises, a workaround is prescribed.
5
Analyze the tanbihat
The first tanbih clarifies that the hadith 'He who digs a well' is general and not restricted; the mention of 'atin is predominant. The second tanbih criticizes a weak explanation in the text.
This reinforces that the ruling applies to all wells, not just 'atin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جگہ تک ہے تو حریم نہ ملنا چاہیے۔ تو ہم نے کہا کہ جس مقدار پر دو حدیثیں متفق ہیں وہاں ہم قیاس کو چھوڑ دیں گے اور جہاں مختلف ہیں وہاں ہم قیاس سے کام لیں گے اور چالیس میں متفق اور ساتھ میں مختلف ہیں تو ہم نے چالیس کو لے لیا ہے۔ تیسری دلیل ... بیر عطن سے کبھی اونٹ کے ذریعہ پانی نکالا جاتا ہے اور کبھی بیر ناضح سے ہاتھ سے پانی نکالا جاتا ہے تو ضرورت دونوں میں برابر ہی لہذ امقدار بھی برابر ہوگی یعنی چالیس ذراع ۔ چوتھی دلیل آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کبھی رشا در از ہو جاتا ہے تو زیادہ جگہ کی حاجت پڑتی ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ ضرورت تو چڑسوں میں پڑے گی رہٹ میں نہیں پڑے گی لہذا اس کو چاہیے کہ رہنٹ سے کام لے۔
تنبیہ پہلی صورت کو عام کہنا محل تأمل ہے کیونکہ اس میں عطن لماشستہ کی قید موجود ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ بیر عطن کا حکم ہے؟
جواب ..... من حفر بيرا عام ہے ہر کنویں کو اس میں کچھ قید نہیں ہے تو یہ دونوں کنوؤں کو شامل ہے اور فـلـه مـمـا حولها اربعون ذراعاً ۔ اسی مطلق بیئر کی جزاء اور حکم ہے اور پھر بعد میں عطن لما شیته فرمانا تقید نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ غالب احوال پر محمول کرتے ہوئے حریم بیر کی منفعت کا ذکر ہے او بیر عطن اور بیر ناضح کے ارد گرد اونٹ وغیرہ بٹھا دیئے جاتے ہیں بالفاظ دیگر یہ تغلیب پر محمول ہے نہ کہ تقیید پر جیسے وذر والبیع میں بھی تغلیب کا لحاظ ہے نہ کہ تقیید کا۔
تنبیه - ۲ مصنف نے ولانه قدیستگی ... الخ ۔ سے جو تعلیل بیان فرمائی ہے علیل ہے اور تصریحات سابقہ کے خلاف ہے نیز اگر ایسا ہو جائے تو اس سے بیر عطن یا بیر ناضح کی حقیقت متغیر نہ ہوگی۔
If the place extends, then the harim should not be given. So we said: On the amount on which the two hadiths agree, we leave qiyas; where they differ, we use qiyas. They agree on forty and differ on a companion, so we took forty. Third proof: From the 'atin well, sometimes water is drawn by camel, and from the nadih well, water is drawn by hand; thus the need in both is equal, so the amount should also be equal, i.e., forty cubits. Fourth proof: You said that sometimes the rope becomes long, so more space is needed. The answer was given: This need arises in bucket-drawn wells, not in pulley wells; therefore, he should use a pulley. Tanbih: Calling the first case general is a point of reflection because it contains the condition 'atin limashta', meaning this is the ruling for the 'atin well? Answer: 'He who digs a well' is general, includes every well, no condition in it; so it includes both wells, and 'for him from around it forty cubits' is the ruling for this absolute well. And afterward specifying 'atin limashta' is not a restriction but rather it is carried on the predominant situation, mentioning the benefit of the well's harim; around the 'atin and nadih wells, camels etc. are placed; in other words, it is carried on predominance not restriction, just as in 'and the export of the sale' predominance is observed, not restriction. Second tanbih: The author's explanation from 'wa lahu qad yastaghiru...' etc. is weak and against previous clarifications; also if this happens, the reality of the 'atin or nadih well does not change.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the harim of a well. The author begins by addressing an objection: if the place extends, no harim should be given. Then he explains the method: for the amount on which two hadiths agree, we leave qiyas; for the amount they differ, we use qiyas. They agree on 40 cubits for the 'atin well but differ on another type, so we take 40. The third proof uses qiyas: since both 'atin and nadih wells are used for drawing water, the need is equal, so the harim should be equal (40 cubits). The fourth proof addresses an objection about long ropes requiring more space; the answer is that this only applies to bucket-drawn wells, so one should use a pulley to avoid extra need. The first tanbih clarifies that the hadith 'He who digs a well' is general; the mention of 'atin limashta' is not a restriction but a predominant case. The second tanbih criticizes the author's own explanation as weak and contradicting earlier clarifications.

Key Terms
حریم (harim): Protected area around a water source that must remain unobstructed.
بیر عطن (bir 'atin): Well from which water is drawn by camel.
بیر ناضح (bir nadih): Well from which water is drawn by hand or pulley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 20 cubits
B) 40 cubits
C) 500 cubits
D) 7 handfuls

Key Takeaway
The harim of a well in the Hanafi school is 40 cubits from each side, established by the agreement of two hadiths and qiyas, with the condition to use a pulley if the rope is long.

Harim of a Spring: 500 Cubits by Tawqif
Explanation of the ruling on spring harim with proof and cubit clarification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the harim of a spring and explain the proof of tawqif.

Core Idea
A spring's harim is 500 cubits from each side, fixed by tawqif.

This lesson explains the ruling on the harim (unused buffer zone) around a natural spring. The author quotes the matn of Quduri and provides commentary, establishing the amount as 500 cubits and emphasizing that this is a textual determination (tawqif). We will examine the ruling, the proof, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is establishing a harim for a spring; the ruling is that it is 500 cubits.
The harim is the area around the spring that cannot be dug or interfered with.
2
Locate the dalil
The author says the estimation is by tawqif, meaning it is based on divine command (hadith), not ijtihad.
Tawqif indicates the ruling is taken from revelation, not analogical reasoning.
3
Note the ikhtilaf on extent
Some early jurists interpreted the 500 cubits as total diameter; the more correct view (al-asahh) is that it is 500 cubits from each side.
The commentary clarifies that the harim extends 500 cubits in every direction from the spring.
4
Identify the cubit type
The cubit used is the fabric cubit (dhira' karbas), also called the Kisrawi or maksara cubit.
The fabric cubit is the standard in Hanafi fiqh for most measurements.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is 500 fabric cubits (approx. 750 feet) per side.
This is the position of al-Hidayah and the majority of later Hanafi texts.

Source Text

چشمہ کے حریم کی مقدار
قال وان كانت عينا فحريمها خمس مائة ذراع لما روينا ولان الحاجة فيه الى زيادة مسافة لان العين تستخرج للزراعة فلابد من موضع يجرى فيه الماء ومن حوض يجمع فيه الماء ومن موضع يجرى فيه الى الزراعة فلهذا يقدر بالزيادة والتقدير بخمس مائة بالتوقيف والاصح انه خمس مائة ذراع من كل جانب كما ذكرنا في العطن والذراع هو المكسرة وقد بيناه من قبل وقيل ان التقدير فى العين والبير بما ذكرناه في اراضيهم لصلابة بها وفى اراضينا رخاوة فيزداد كيلا يتحول الماء الى الثاني فيتعطل الاول ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر وہ چشمہ ہو تو اس کا حریم پانچ ذراع ہے اس دلیل سے جو کہ ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور اس لئے کہ اس میں زیادہ مساحت کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے کہ چشمہ زراعت کے لئے نکالا جاتا ہے تو ضروری ہے ایسی جگہ کا ہونا جس میں پانی چل سکے اور ایسے حوض کا ہونا جس میں پانی جمع ہو سکے اور ایسی جگہ کا ہونا جس کے اندر کو پانی کھیتی تک پہنچے اسی وجہ سے اس کو زیادتی کے ساتھ مقدر کیا گیا ہے اور پانچ سو کے ساتھ تقدیر تو قیفی ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ پانچ سو ذراع ہر جانب سے ہے جیسا کہ ہم عطن میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور ذراع وہ کسروی ذراع ہے اور اس کو ہم ماقبل میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور کہا گیا ہے کہ چشمہ اور کنویں میں وہ تقدیر جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے یہ ان کی زمینوں میں ہے اس میں سختی ہونے کی وجہ سے ہماری زمینوں میں نرمی ہے۔ تو تقدیر زیادہ ہو جائے گی تا کہ دوسرے کی جانب پانی بہ ہونے کہ پہلا معطل ہو جائے ۔
تشریح پہلے میں کا حریم بتایا گیا ہے اور یہ چشمہ کے حریم کی مقدار ہے یعنی پانچ سو ذراع کیونکہ اس میں زیادہ جگہ کی ضرورت ہے جو متن سے واضح ہے۔
یہاں یہ سوال ہوسکتا تھا کہ پھر کنویں کے اندر بھی زیادہ کی حاجت ہو سکتی ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ چشمہ کی یہ مقدار تو قیفی ہے جیسا کہ حدیث مذکور سے ثابت ہے حسب سابق یہاں بھی پانچ سو ذراع ہر ہر جانب سے مراد ہے پھر یہاں ذراع سے ذراع کر باس مراد ہے جس کو ذراع کسروی بھی کہا جاتا ہے اس کو مکسرہ سے تعبیر فرمایا گیا ہے جس کو دہ دردہ کے مسئلہ میں مصنف نے بیان فرمایا ہے پھر مصنف نے فرمایا کہ بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ مذکورہ عرب کی سخت زمین میں ہے کہ وہاں کی زمین سخت ہے رہی ہماری زمین تو وہ نرم ہے اس میں حسب ضرورت زیادہ حریم دیا جائے گا تا کہ کنواں یا چشمہ معطل نہ ہو جائے۔
تنبیہ - عرب کے اندر دو قسم کے ذراع مستعمل تھے ایک ذراع کر باس ( کپڑے ناپنے کا گز ) دوسرا ذراع مساحت ( زمین وغیرہ ناپنے کا گز ) ذراع مساحت حسب تصریح قاضی خان وغیرہ سات مشت کا ہے جس میں ہر سٹھی انگوٹھا کھڑا ہو کذافی البهر الرائق ص ۱۸۷ج ا - اور یہ بھی جس پر انگوٹھا کھڑا ہو آجکل کی پیمائش کے حساب سے چھ انچ ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اس طرح کی دو مٹھی کافٹ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ذراع مساحت ساڑھے تین فٹ یا بیالیس انچ کا ہوتا ہے جو انگریزی گز سے چھ انچ زیادہ ہے۔ لیکن فقہاء کے کلام میں عموما جس جگہ لفظ ذراع بولا گیا ہے ذراع مساحت مراد نہیں بلکہ ذراع کر باس مراد ہوتا ہے اور بعض مواضع میں فقہاء کا اختلاف بھی ہے کہ بعض نے اس میں ذراع کر باس مراد لیا ہے اور بعض نے ذراع مساحت جیسا کہ ماء کثیر کی بحث میں ۔ اور دہ دردہ کی تعیین میں قاضی خان نے ذراع مسباحت کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ لیکن جمہور فقہاء جیسے ہدایہ اور عام متون شروح نے اس جگہ بھی ذراع کر باس ہی کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے اور ذراع کر باس بھی دو قسم کا مشہور ہے۔ متقدمین میں بتیس انگشت کا ذراع معروف ہے اور متاخرین میں چوبیس انگشت کا انگشت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ چار انگلیاں ملا کر رکھی جائیں اور انگوٹھا ان کے ساتھ شامل نہ کیا جائے۔ پھر چار ان کے برابر اور پھر اسی طرح چار یہاں تک کہ ۲۴/۳۲ / ہو جائیں اور چونکہ ایک مشت (مٹھی) بھی چار انگشت کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے متقدمین کا ذراع آٹھ مشت (مٹھی) اور متاخرین کا چھ مشت ہو گا عام کتب مذہب متون و شروح اور فتاوی متاخرین کا ذراع مستعمل ہے اس پر حسابات شرعیہ قائم کئے گئے ہیں یعنی چھ مشت یا ۲۴ انگشت کا ایک ذراع و بحث فی العالمگیر ہیں ۱۸۸ ج او فی البحرص ۸۰ ج ۱ ص ۱۴۷ ج ا جن سے یہ واضح ہوتا ہے کہ پانی کی مساحت کے متعلق وہ دردہ کے مسئلہ میں ذراع کرباس معتبر ہے اور اس کی صحیح اورانج پیمائش ۲۴ انگلیاں ہیں یا ۶ یہ بعینہ وہ مقدار ہے جس کو ہمارے عرف میں ایک ہاتھ کہا جاتا ہے جس کی تفصیل ص ۱۹۱ ج اپر ہے وہاں کی عبارت سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بحر کی بحث المیاہ میں جو قول دلو الجی نقل کیا ہے کہ سات مشت کا ایک ذراع ہوتا ہے یہ اس قدیم ذراع کی پیمائش ہے جو آخری کسرای ملک فارس کا ذراع اور اسلام میں عام طور پر جو ذراع رائج ہو اور وہ ایک مٹھی کم یعنی ۶ مٹھی یا ۲۴ انگلیوں کا ذراع ہے اور یہی معتبر ہے اور عرب اور فقہاء کی سزاجت و سادگی کا بھی یہی مختصیٰ ہے کہ ان کے کلام میں ذراع سے مراد یہی ذراع ہو کیونکہ وہ ذراع طبیعی ایک ہاتھ ) کی صحیح مقدار ہے اور یہ ذراع انگریزی گز سے نصف یعنی ڈیڑھ فٹ یا ۱۸ اینچ ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ عام طور پر چکرورتی (علم
The amount of the harim of a spring. He said: If it is a spring, then its harim is five hundred cubits, due to what we narrated, and because the need for more area; because the spring is dug for agriculture, so there must be a place for water to flow, a basin to collect water, and a place for water to reach the cultivation; therefore it is estimated with increase, and the estimation as five hundred is by tawqif (textual determination). And the more correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side as we mentioned for the 'atin. And the cubit is the maksara (broken) cubit which we have explained before. And it is said that the estimation for the spring and well as we mentioned is in their lands due to hardness; but in our lands, there is softness, so the amount increases so that water does not shift to the second [well] causing the first to be idle. Translation of Quduri's text: The author said: And if it is a spring, then its harim is five hundred cubits, due to the proof we narrated, and because the need for more area; because the spring is dug for agriculture, so it is necessary to have a place where water can flow, a basin to collect water, and a place where water reaches the cultivation; for this reason it is estimated with increase, and the estimation with five hundred is by tawqif. And the more correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side, as we explained in the 'atin. And the cubit is the Kisrawi cubit, which we have explained before. And it is said that the estimation for the spring and well as we mentioned is in their lands due to hardness; in our lands, there is softness, so the amount increases so that water does not shift to the second [well] causing the first to be idle. Explanation: The harim of the first [well] was mentioned; and this is the amount of the spring's harim, i.e., five hundred cubits, because more space is needed, which is clear from the text. Here a question could arise: Then for wells also more may be needed? The answer was given: This amount for the spring is by tawqif, as proven by the mentioned hadith; as before, here also five hundred cubits from each side is intended. Then here by cubit is meant the fabric cubit (dhira' karbas) which is also called Kisrawi cubit; it is expressed as maksara. The author has explained it in the issue of 'dah dardah'. Then the author said that some jurists said that the mentioned [amount] is for the hard land of Arabia; our land is soft; in it, more harim will be given according to need so that the well or spring does not become idle. Tanbih: In Arabia, two types of cubits were used: one is the fabric cubit (dhira' karbas) and the other is the surveying cubit (dhira' misaha). The surveying cubit, according to the specification of Qadikhan etc., is seven handfuls, in which each handful has the thumb standing; as in Bahr al-Ra'iq vol.1 p.187. And this thumb standing is six inches in today's measurement, because two such handfuls make a foot. From this it is understood that the surveying cubit is 3.5 feet or 42 inches, which is six inches more than the English yard. But generally in the words of jurists, wherever the word 'dhira'' is used, it refers to the fabric cubit, not the surveying cubit. And in some places, there is difference among jurists: some took the fabric cubit and some the surveying cubit, as in the discussion of abundant water. And in the determination of 'dah dardah', Qadikhan chose the surveying cubit. But the majority of jurists like Hidayah and common texts and commentaries have considered even here the fabric cubit as correct. And the fabric cubit is also of two famous types: among the early scholars, the cubit of 32 finger-widths is known; among the later scholars, the cubit of 24 finger-widths. By finger-width is meant four fingers placed together, thumb not included. Then four [fingers] equal to that, and so on until 24/32 become. And since one handful (mushth) is also four fingers, the early scholars' cubit is eight handfuls, and the later scholars' cubit is six handfuls. The cubit used in the common books of the madhhab, texts, commentaries, and fatwas of the later scholars is the one on which shari calculations are based, i.e., six handfuls or 24 fingers, as discussed in al-'Alamghiri vol.1 p.188 and in al-Bahr vol.1 p.80 and p.147, from which it is clear that regarding water measurement in the issue of 'dah dardah', the fabric cubit is reliable, and its correct measurement is 24 fingers or 6 handfuls; it is exactly the amount called 'one hand' in our common usage, which is detailed on p.191 vol.1. From the text there, it is also known that in the discussion of water in al-Bahr, the statement quoted from Dalu al-Ji that one cubit is seven handfuls is the measurement of the old cubit, which was the cubit of the last Kisra of Persia, and the cubit commonly used in Islam is one handful less, i.e., 6 handfuls or 24 fingers, and this is reliable. And it is befitting the simplicity and austerity of the Arabs and jurists that in their words, 'dhira'' refers to this cubit, because that is the correct measurement of the natural cubit (one hand). And this cubit is half of the English yard, i.e., 1.5 feet or 18 inches, as is commonly [known].
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage explains the harim of a spring. The author states it is 500 cubits, based on tawqif (textual determination) and the need for agriculture. The more correct view is that the amount is from each side. The cubit used is the 'maksara' cubit, also called Kisrawi or fabric cubit. An objection about wells needing more is addressed: the spring's amount is fixed by tawqif. Then the discussion shifts to the types of cubits. The fabric cubit is the standard used by majority of Hanafi jurists, with two variants: 32 fingers (early) and 24 fingers (later). The relied-upon measurement is 24 fingers or 6 handfuls, which equals approximately 18 inches. The surveying cubit (7 handfuls, 42 inches) is not used in fiqh rulings except in some specific contexts like Qadikhan's view on 'dah dardah'. The text concludes that the natural hand cubit (6 handfuls) is the correct one.

Key Terms
عین ('ayn): A natural spring of water.
ذراع (dhira'): Cubit, a unit of length. In this lesson, primarily the fabric cubit.
توقيف (tawqif): A ruling based on divine text, not human reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct view (al-asahh) in the Hanafi school, what is the harim of a spring?
A) 500 cubits total diameter
B) 500 cubits from each side
C) 40 cubits from each side
D) 500 cubits from one side only

Key Takeaway
The harim of a spring is 500 fabric cubits from each side, established by tawqif, and is a wajib right of the owner.

Determining the Cubit: Fabric Cubit as the Hanafi Standard
Detailed determination of the cubit measurement for fiqh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the fabric cubit and surveying cubit in Hanafi fiqh and identify the standard cubit used in harim measurements.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school uses the fabric cubit (24 fingers, 18 inches) for fiqh measurements, not the surveying cubit.

This lesson delves into the precise measurement of the cubit (dhira') as used in Hanafi fiqh, particularly for harim. The passage clarifies that the 'maksara' cubit is the fabric cubit, also known as the Kisrawi cubit. We will explore the two types of cubits, the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the surveying cubit, and the final authoritative measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of cubits
Fabric cubit (dhira' karbas) used for cloth and generally in fiqh; surveying cubit (dhira' misaha) used for land measurement.
The surveying cubit is larger (7 handfuls) and used in specific contexts like 'dah dardah'.
2
Understand the measurement of the fabric cubit
The relied-upon fabric cubit consists of 6 handfuls (mushth) or 24 finger-widths (angusht). A handful is 4 fingers placed together, excluding thumb.
Later scholars standardized at 24 fingers; early scholars used 32 fingers (8 handfuls).
3
Identify the surveying cubit
The surveying cubit is 7 handfuls (42 inches), as per Qadikhan and others.
This cubit is not standard in fiqh rulings except in limited contexts.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi jurists (e.g., Qadikhan) used the surveying cubit in the issue of 'dah dardah'; the majority (Hidayah, etc.) use the fabric cubit.
The thamarah al-khilaf is a significant difference in length: 500 fabric cubits vs 500 surveying cubits.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon cubit for harim and most fiqh rulings is the fabric cubit of 24 fingers (6 handfuls), approximately 18 inches.
This is consistent with the natural hand cubit and the practice of the majority of Hanafi scholars.

تشریح پہلے میں کا حریم بتایا گیا ہے اور یہ چشمہ کے حریم کی مقدار ہے یعنی پانچ سو ذراع کیونکہ اس میں زیادہ جگہ کی ضرورت ہے جو متن سے واضح ہے۔
یہاں یہ سوال ہوسکتا تھا کہ پھر کنویں کے اندر بھی زیادہ کی حاجت ہو سکتی ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ چشمہ کی یہ مقدار تو قیفی ہے جیسا کہ حدیث مذکور سے ثابت ہے حسب سابق یہاں بھی پانچ سو ذراع ہر ہر جانب سے مراد ہے پھر یہاں ذراع سے ذراع کر باس مراد ہے جس کو ذراع کسروی بھی کہا جاتا ہے اس کو مکسرہ سے تعبیر فرمایا گیا ہے جس کو دہ دردہ کے مسئلہ میں مصنف نے بیان فرمایا ہے پھر مصنف نے فرمایا کہ بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ مذکورہ عرب کی سخت زمین میں ہے کہ وہاں کی زمین سخت ہے رہی ہماری زمین تو وہ نرم ہے اس میں حسب ضرورت زیادہ حریم دیا جائے گا تا کہ کنواں یا چشمہ معطل نہ ہو جائے۔
تنبیہ - عرب کے اندر دو قسم کے ذراع مستعمل تھے ایک ذراع کر باس ( کپڑے ناپنے کا گز ) دوسرا ذراع مساحت ( زمین وغیرہ ناپنے کا گز ) ذراع مساحت حسب تصریح قاضی خان وغیرہ سات مشت کا ہے جس میں ہر سٹھی انگوٹھا کھڑا ہو کذافی البهر الرائق ص ۱۸۷ج ا - اور یہ بھی جس پر انگوٹھا کھڑا ہو آجکل کی پیمائش کے حساب سے چھ انچ ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اس طرح کی دو مٹھی کافٹ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ذراع مساحت ساڑھے تین فٹ یا بیالیس انچ کا ہوتا ہے جو انگریزی گز سے چھ انچ زیادہ ہے۔ لیکن فقہاء کے کلام میں عموما جس جگہ لفظ ذراع بولا گیا ہے ذراع مساحت مراد نہیں بلکہ ذراع کر باس مراد ہوتا ہے اور بعض مواضع میں فقہاء کا اختلاف بھی ہے کہ بعض نے اس میں ذراع کر باس مراد لیا ہے اور بعض نے ذراع مساحت جیسا کہ ماء کثیر کی بحث میں ۔ اور دہ دردہ کی تعیین میں قاضی خان نے ذراع مسباحت کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ لیکن جمہور فقہاء جیسے ہدایہ اور عام متون شروح نے اس جگہ بھی ذراع کر باس ہی کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے اور ذراع کر باس بھی دو قسم کا مشہور ہے۔ متقدمین میں بتیس انگشت کا ذراع معروف ہے اور متاخرین میں چوبیس انگشت کا انگشت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ چار انگلیاں ملا کر رکھی جائیں اور انگوٹھا ان کے ساتھ شامل نہ کیا جائے۔ پھر چار ان کے برابر اور پھر اسی طرح چار یہاں تک کہ ۲۴/۳۲ / ہو جائیں اور چونکہ ایک مشت (مٹھی) بھی چار انگشت کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے متقدمین کا ذراع آٹھ مشت (مٹھی) اور متاخرین کا چھ مشت ہو گا عام کتب مذہب متون و شروح اور فتاوی متاخرین کا ذراع مستعمل ہے اس پر حسابات شرعیہ قائم کئے گئے ہیں یعنی چھ مشت یا ۲۴ انگشت کا ایک ذراع و بحث فی العالمگیر ہیں ۱۸۸ ج او فی البحرص ۸۰ ج ۱ ص ۱۴۷ ج ا جن سے یہ واضح ہوتا ہے کہ پانی کی مساحت کے متعلق وہ دردہ کے مسئلہ میں ذراع کرباس معتبر ہے اور اس کی صحیح اورانج پیمائش ۲۴ انگلیاں ہیں یا ۶ یہ بعینہ وہ مقدار ہے جس کو ہمارے عرف میں ایک ہاتھ کہا جاتا ہے جس کی تفصیل ص ۱۹۱ ج اپر ہے وہاں کی عبارت سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بحر کی بحث المیاہ میں جو قول دلو الجی نقل کیا ہے کہ سات مشت کا ایک ذراع ہوتا ہے یہ اس قدیم ذراع کی پیمائش ہے جو آخری کسرای ملک فارس کا ذراع اور اسلام میں عام طور پر جو ذراع رائج ہو اور وہ ایک مٹھی کم یعنی ۶ مٹھی یا ۲۴ انگلیوں کا ذراع ہے اور یہی معتبر ہے اور عرب اور فقہاء کی سزاجت و سادگی کا بھی یہی مختصیٰ ہے کہ ان کے کلام میں ذراع سے مراد یہی ذراع ہو کیونکہ وہ ذراع طبیعی ایک ہاتھ ) کی صحیح مقدار ہے اور یہ ذراع انگریزی گز سے نصف یعنی ڈیڑھ فٹ یا ۱۸ اینچ ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ عام طور پر چکرورتی (علم
The amount of the harim of a spring. He said: If it is a spring, then its harim is five hundred cubits, due to what we narrated, and because the need for more area; because the spring is dug for agriculture, so there must be a place for water to flow, a basin to collect water, and a place for water to reach the cultivation; therefore it is estimated with increase, and the estimation as five hundred is by tawqif (textual determination). And the more correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side as we mentioned for the 'atin. And the cubit is the maksara (broken) cubit which we have explained before. And it is said that the estimation for the spring and well as we mentioned is in their lands due to hardness; but in our lands, there is softness, so the amount increases so that water does not shift to the second [well] causing the first to be idle. Translation of Quduri's text: The author said: And if it is a spring, then its harim is five hundred cubits, due to the proof we narrated, and because the need for more area; because the spring is dug for agriculture, so it is necessary to have a place where water can flow, a basin to collect water, and a place where water reaches the cultivation; for this reason it is estimated with increase, and the estimation with five hundred is by tawqif. And the more correct view is that it is five hundred cubits from each side, as we explained in the 'atin. And the cubit is the Kisrawi cubit, which we have explained before. And it is said that the estimation for the spring and well as we mentioned is in their lands due to hardness; in our lands, there is softness, so the amount increases so that water does not shift to the second [well] causing the first to be idle. Explanation: The harim of the first [well] was mentioned; and this is the amount of the spring's harim, i.e., five hundred cubits, because more space is needed, which is clear from the text. Here a question could arise: Then for wells also more may be needed? The answer was given: This amount for the spring is by tawqif, as proven by the mentioned hadith; as before, here also five hundred cubits from each side is intended. Then here by cubit is meant the fabric cubit (dhira' karbas) which is also called Kisrawi cubit; it is expressed as maksara. The author has explained it in the issue of 'dah dardah'. Then the author said that some jurists said that the mentioned [amount] is for the hard land of Arabia; our land is soft; in it, more harim will be given according to need so that the well or spring does not become idle. Tanbih: In Arabia, two types of cubits were used: one is the fabric cubit (dhira' karbas) and the other is the surveying cubit (dhira' misaha). The surveying cubit, according to the specification of Qadikhan etc., is seven handfuls, in which each handful has the thumb standing; as in Bahr al-Ra'iq vol.1 p.187. And this thumb standing is six inches in today's measurement, because two such handfuls make a foot. From this it is understood that the surveying cubit is 3.5 feet or 42 inches, which is six inches more than the English yard. But generally in the words of jurists, wherever the word 'dhira'' is used, it refers to the fabric cubit, not the surveying cubit. And in some places, there is difference among jurists: some took the fabric cubit and some the surveying cubit, as in the discussion of abundant water. And in the determination of 'dah dardah', Qadikhan chose the surveying cubit. But the majority of jurists like Hidayah and common texts and commentaries have considered even here the fabric cubit as correct. And the fabric cubit is also of two famous types: among the early scholars, the cubit of 32 finger-widths is known; among the later scholars, the cubit of 24 finger-widths. By finger-width is meant four fingers placed together, thumb not included. Then four [fingers] equal to that, and so on until 24/32 become. And since one handful (mushth) is also four fingers, the early scholars' cubit is eight handfuls, and the later scholars' cubit is six handfuls. The cubit used in the common books of the madhhab, texts, commentaries, and fatwas of the later scholars is the one on which shari calculations are based, i.e., six handfuls or 24 fingers, as discussed in al-'Alamghiri vol.1 p.188 and in al-Bahr vol.1 p.80 and p.147, from which it is clear that regarding water measurement in the issue of 'dah dardah', the fabric cubit is reliable, and its correct measurement is 24 fingers or 6 handfuls; it is exactly the amount called 'one hand' in our common usage, which is detailed on p.191 vol.1. From the text there, it is also known that in the discussion of water in al-Bahr, the statement quoted from Dalu al-Ji that one cubit is seven handfuls is the measurement of the old cubit, which was the cubit of the last Kisra of Persia, and the cubit commonly used in Islam is one handful less, i.e., 6 handfuls or 24 fingers, and this is reliable. And it is befitting the simplicity and austerity of the Arabs and jurists that in their words, 'dhira'' refers to this cubit, because that is the correct measurement of the natural cubit (one hand). And this cubit is half of the English yard, i.e., 1.5 feet or 18 inches, as is commonly [known].
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage explains the harim of a spring. The author states it is 500 cubits, based on tawqif (textual determination) and the need for agriculture. The more correct view is that the amount is from each side. The cubit used is the 'maksara' cubit, also called Kisrawi or fabric cubit. An objection about wells needing more is addressed: the spring's amount is fixed by tawqif. Then the discussion shifts to the types of cubits. The fabric cubit is the standard used by majority of Hanafi jurists, with two variants: 32 fingers (early) and 24 fingers (later). The relied-upon measurement is 24 fingers or 6 handfuls, which equals approximately 18 inches. The surveying cubit (7 handfuls, 42 inches) is not used in fiqh rulings except in some specific contexts like Qadikhan's view on 'dah dardah'. The text concludes that the natural hand cubit (6 handfuls) is the correct one.

Key Terms
ذراع کرباس (dhira' karbas): Fabric cubit, used for cloth; the standard in Hanafi fiqh.
ذراع مساحت (dhira' misaha): Surveying cubit, used for land; 7 handfuls.
مشت (mushth): Handful, a measure of four fingers placed together (excluding thumb).
انگشت (angusht): Finger-width, the width of four fingers placed together.
دہ دردہ (dah dardah): A specific issue in Hanafi fiqh concerning water distribution or measurement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi jurists, how many handfuls (mushth) make up the standard cubit used in harim measurements?
A) 7 handfuls
B) 6 handfuls
C) 8 handfuls
D) 5 handfuls

Key Takeaway
The standard Hanafi cubit for harim and most fiqh rulings is the fabric cubit of 6 handfuls (24 finger-widths), approximately 18 inches.

6 min
The Harim of a Spring and the Standard Cubit (Dira' Karbas)
Defines harim of spring and clarifies cubit measurement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the harim of a spring and identify the relied-upon cubit measurement, applying it to determine the protected area.

Core Idea
The harim of a spring is 500 cloth cubits per side; the cloth cubit is 6 fists or 24 fingers (18 inches).

Previously, the harim of a well was discussed. Now the author turns to springs, which require more space. This passage defines the harim of a spring as 500 cubits on each side, based on a hadith. It also clarifies a critical point: which cubit is intended? The author resolves the question by adopting the cloth cubit (dira' karbas), explaining its measurement and emphasizing that this is the standard for all water-related issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The harim of a spring is 500 cubits on each side. This is from a hadith (dalil naqli). Understand that this is the base measure.
The same measure applies to wells in other contexts.
2
Recognize the flexibility for land type
The text states that for soft land, the harim may be increased to prevent the spring from being rendered useless. This is an application of the principle of necessity.
The increase is discretionary by a judge.
3
Distinguish between the two cubits
Two cubits were used in Arabia: the cloth cubit (dira' karbas) and the surveying cubit (dira' misaha). The surveying cubit is larger (7 fists, ~42 inches).
Common confusion arises when the word 'dira' is used without qualification.
4
Determine the authoritative cubit
The majority of Hanafi jurists, including the author of Hidayah, adopt the cloth cubit. It is the natural cubit (6 fists, 24 fingers, ~18 inches). This is the mufta bihi view.
Qadi Khan used the surveying cubit in some issues, but the majority view prevails.
5
Apply the measurement
The harim is 500 cloth cubits on each side. One cloth cubit = 1.5 feet, so the harim extends 750 feet in each direction from the spring.
This calculation assumes standard English conversion.

کی سزاجت و سادگی کا بھی یہی مختصیٰ ہے کہ ان کے کلام میں ذراع سے مراد یہی ذراع ہو کیونکہ وہ ذراع طبیعی ایک ہاتھ ) کی صحیح مقدار ہے اور یہ ذراع انگریزی گز سے نصف یعنی ڈیڑھ فٹ یا ۱۸ اینچ ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ عام طور پر چکرورتی (علم حساب میں اس کی تصریح الفاظ ذیل میں موجود ہیں۔ ۱۹اینچ یعنی ایک بالشت ۲ بالشت یعنی ۱۸ اینچ یا ایک ہاتھ ۔ ۲ ہاتھ یعنی ایک گز ، ایک گز یعنی ۳ فٹ یا ۳۲ اینچ خلاصہ یہ کہ رائج الوقت انگریزی گز اور فٹ کے اعتبار سے ذراع مساحت ایک گز اور چھ انچ ہے یا ساڑھے تین فٹ یا بیالیس انچ اور ذراع کر باس نصف گز ، یا ڈیڑھ فٹ، یا ۱۸ اینچ ہے تو جس طرح پانی کے مسائل میں ذراع کر باس معتبر ہے ایسے ہی حریم کے اندر بھی ذراع کر باس معتبر ہے یہی ذراع کر باس ہے اور یہی ذراع کسروی ہے اور یہی ذراع کمر ہے۔
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. Due to hardness in that land, our lands have softness, so the measure will be increased so that the water does not flow to the other side and the first becomes disabled. Commentary: Previously, the harim of a well was explained. This is the measure of the harim of a spring, i.e., five hundred cubits because it needs more space, which is clear from the text. Here a question could arise: can a well also need more? The answer given is that this measure for a spring is fixed as proven from the mentioned hadith. Similarly, here also five hundred cubits on each side is meant. Then here the cubit intended is the cloth cubit (dira' karbas), also called the Kisra cubit. It is described as 'maksarah' which the author explained in the issue of 'dah darda'. Then the author said that some jurists say that the mentioned (measure) is for the hard land of Arabia; as for our land, it is soft, so a larger harim will be given as needed so that the well or spring is not rendered useless. Note: In Arabia, two types of cubits were used: the cloth cubit (for measuring cloth) and the surveying cubit (for measuring land, etc.). According to Qadi Khan and others, the surveying cubit is seven fists, with each thumb standing upright, as in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol.1 p.187. Also, that in which the thumb stands upright, by today's measurement, is six inches because two such fists make a foot. This shows that the surveying cubit is three and a half feet or forty-two inches, which is six inches more than the English yard. But generally, wherever the word 'dira' is used in the jurists' speech, the surveying cubit is not meant but the cloth cubit is meant. In some places there is disagreement among jurists: some take it as the cloth cubit and some as the surveying cubit, like in the discussion of abundant water. In determining the 'dah darda', Qadi Khan adopted the surveying cubit. But the majority of jurists like the Hidayah and common texts and commentaries have declared the cloth cubit to be correct even in this place. The cloth cubit is also of two famous types: among the earlier scholars, a cubit of thirty-two fingers is known; among the later scholars, twenty-four fingers. By 'finger' is meant that four fingers are placed together and the thumb is not included. Then four (fingers) equal one fist, and so on until 24/32. Since one fist is also four fingers, the earlier scholars' cubit is eight fists and the later scholars' is six fists. The commonly used cubit in the books of the school, texts, commentaries, and fatwas of the later scholars is six fists or twenty-four fingers. This is established for legal calculations, as in al-`Alamghiri vol.1 p.188, al-Bahr vol.1 p.80 and p.147. From this it is clear that for water measurement, the cloth cubit is relied upon in the issue of 'dah darda', and its correct and final measurement is 24 fingers or 6 fists. It is exactly the amount that in our custom is called one handspan, whose detail is on page 191. From the text there, it is also known that the statement in al-Bahr's discussion of waters that a cubit is seven fists is a measurement of the ancient cubit which was the cubit of the last Chosroes of Persia and which was commonly prevalent in Islam; and that (the later) cubit, which is one fist less, i.e., 6 fists or 24 fingers, is the reliable one. And this is what is consistent with the simplicity and plainness of the Arabs and jurists, that by 'dira' in their speech this cubit is meant, because it is the correct measure of the natural cubit (one handspan). And this cubit is half the English yard, i.e., one and a half feet or 18 inches. As generally clarified in the science of geometry, the words exist: 19 inches = one span, 2 spans = 18 inches or one hand, 2 hands = one yard, one yard = 3 feet or 36 inches. In summary, according to the currently prevalent English yard and foot, the surveying cubit is one yard and six inches, or three and a half feet, or 42 inches; and the cloth cubit is half a yard, or one and a half feet, or 18 inches. So just as for water issues the cloth cubit is reliable, similarly in the harim the cloth cubit is reliable. This is the cloth cubit, this is the Kisra cubit, and this is the cubit of the forearm.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage defines the harim (protected area) for a spring. The author states that the harim is 500 cubits on each side, based on a hadith. However, for soft land, the measure may be increased to ensure the spring is not rendered useless. The passage then clarifies the type of cubit (dira') used: it is the 'dira' karbas' (cloth cubit), also called 'dira' kasrawi'. This is distinct from the 'dira' misaha' (surveying cubit) which is larger. The relied-upon view among later Hanafi scholars is the 6-fist/24-finger cubit, which is about 18 inches. The passage emphasizes that this is the standard for all water-related measurements and the harim.

Key Terms
حریم (harim): The protected area around a well or spring that is necessary for its use and is owned by the well owner.
ذراع کرباس (dira' karbas): The cloth cubit, a unit of length equal to 24 fingers (6 fists), used for measuring in Hanafi fiqh for water and harim issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 500 surveyor's cubits (dira' misaha)
B) 500 cloth cubits (dira' karbas) on each side
C) 7 fists per cubit
D) 32 fingers per cubit

Key Takeaway
The harim of a spring is 500 cloth cubits (6 fists/24 fingers) per side, with flexibility for soft land; this is the mufta bihi view.

Well Dug in Another's Harim: The Two Hanafi Views
Explains the owner's options when a well is dug in his harim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the remedy when a well is dug in another's harim and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view with its basis.

Core Idea
When a well is dug in another's harim, the trespasser must compensate the owner for the decrease in value—the owner then fills it himself.

In this passage, we encounter a practical scenario from Hanafi property law: someone digs a well on another's land (within the harim). The owner has a choice: he may fill it himself as a favour, or he may enforce a remedy. The Hanafi jurists discuss two possible remedies: forcing the trespasser to fill it, or requiring compensation and letting the owner fill it. Let's examine the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the owner's two options
The passage begins by stating that if someone digs a well in another's harim, the owner may fill it himself as a favor (tabarru'an). If he wants to enforce his right, there are two views.
Harim is the buffer zone around a well, typically 40 cubits.
2
Examine the first view: force the trespasser to fill
One view says the owner can compel the trespasser to fill the well, drawing an analogy to throwing garbage in another's house—the trespasser must remove it.
This view sees the trespass as an ongoing violation that must be undone by the trespasser.
3
Examine the second view: compensation and owner fills
The second view says the trespasser must guarantee the decrease in value (nuqsan) caused to the land, and then the owner fills it. This is analogized to someone who demolishes another's wall—he pays damages.
This view focuses on compensation rather than specific performance.
4
Determine the tarjih
The text states 'وهذا هو الصحيح' (this is the correct view) for the second view, citing al-Khassaf's Adab al-Qadi. So the mufta bihi is compensation.
The tarjih is based on practical considerations and authority of later Hanafi works.
5
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The underlying legal principle is that the owner's right to his land includes the right to have it restored to its original condition. However, forcing the trespasser to fill may be impractical or lead to further damage, so compensation is preferred.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of 'daman al-ajza' (liability for parts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی کی جریم میں کنواں کھود دیا اس کا کیا حکم ۔
فان احتفر آخر بيرا فى حد حريم الاولى للاول ان يصلحه ويكبسه تبرعا ولو اراد اخذ الثاني فيه قيل له ان ياخذه بكبسه لان ازالة جناية حفره به كما فى الكناسة يلقها فى دار غيره فانه يؤخذ برفعها وقيل يضمنه النقصان ثم يكبسه بنفسه كما اذا هدم چدار غيره وهذا هو الصحيح ذكره في ادب القاضي للخصاف رفة الـ
ترجمہ پس اگر دوسرے نے اول کے حریم میں کنواں کھودا تو اول کو حق ہے کہ وہ بطور احسان کے اس کو پاٹ دے اور اگر وہ اس میں دوسرے سے مواخذہ کرنا چاہے تو کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کو اس کا حق ہے کہ وہ اس کو اس کے پاٹنے میں ماخوذ کرے اس لئے کہ اس کے کنواں کھود نے کے جرم کا ازالہ اسی سے ہوگا جیسے کوڑے میں جس کو کوئی دوسرے کے گھر میں ڈال دے تو وہ اس کے اٹھانے میں ماخوذ ہوگا اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کو نقصان کا ضامن بنا دے پھر اس کو خود پاٹ دے جیسے کسی نے دوسرے کی دیوار گرادی اور یہی صحیح ہے جس کو خصاف نے ادب القاضی میں بیان کیا ہے اور نقصان کے پہچانے کے طریقہ کو ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح اگر دوسرے نے اس کے حریم میں کنواں کھود بھی لیا تو اب اول کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ دوسرے پر احسان کرے اور اس کے پاٹنے میں دوسرے کی مدد کرے۔ اور اگر احسان و تبرع نہ کرے بلکہ اس سے مواخذہ کرے تو اب دو قول ہیں
What is the ruling if someone has dug a well in another's harim? If another digs a well within the boundary of the harim of the first, the first has the right to repair it and fill it as a favor. And if he wants to hold the second to account, it is said that he has the right to make him fill it, because removing the crime of his digging is achieved by that, like when someone throws garbage in another's house, he is taken to remove it. And it is said that he (the second) should guarantee the decrease in value, then the first fills it himself, just as if someone demolished another's wall. And this is the correct view, mentioned by al-Khassaf in Adab al-Qadi. Translation: So if the second dug a well in the first's harim, the first has the right to fill it as a favor. And if he wants to take the second to account, there are two views: one is that he can force the second to fill it, because the removal of the crime is by his action, like garbage thrown in another's house. The other is that he makes him guarantee the decrease in value and then the first fills it himself, like demolishing a wall. This (second) is the correct view as stated by al-Khassaf in Adab al-Qadi. Commentary: If the second dug a well in the first's harim, the first has the option to do a favor and help the second fill it. If he does not do a favor but takes action, there are two opinions.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a well has already been dug in another's harim. It gives the owner (first) two possible courses. First, he may choose to fill the well himself as an act of charity (tabarru'), helping the trespasser. Second, if he wants to enforce his right, there are two views within the Hanafi school: (a) The trespasser can be forced to fill the well, analogized to someone who throws garbage into another's house—he must remove it. (b) The trespasser must compensate the owner for the decrease in value (due to the damage to the land), and then the owner fills it himself, analogized to someone who demolishes another's wall. The text declares the second view to be the correct (sahih) one, as recorded by al-Khassaf in Adab al-Qadi. The commentary notes that after filling, the method of assessing the decrease in value is also discussed but not detailed here.

Key Terms
تبرعا (tabarru'an): Acting voluntarily as a favor, without expectation of compensation.
يضمنه النقصان (yadmanuhu al-nuqsan): He guarantees the decrease in value (the damage caused to the property).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct (sahih) ruling according to the text when a well is dug in another's harim?
A) The trespasser must fill the well himself.
B) The owner must fill the well as a favor.
C) The trespasser must compensate the owner for the decrease in value and then the owner fills the well.
D) The trespasser must pay a fine to the state.

Key Takeaway
When a well is dug in another's harim without permission, the relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that the trespasser must compensate the owner for the decrease in land value, and the owner then fills the well.

Compensation for Damage to a Well by Digging a Second Well
Ruling on compensation for damage to a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a second well damages an existing well and apply the method of calculating compensation.

Core Idea
Harm must be removed and loss compensated: the digger of a damaging well must fill it and pay for the decrease in the value of the first well.

This lesson addresses a specific case from the chapter on reviving dead lands (Ihya al-Mawat): what happens when a person digs a second well that damages a pre-existing well? The Hanafi school offers two opinions, and the preferred view requires both filling the well and compensating for the loss in value. Understanding this ruling illustrates the broader Hanafi principle of removing harm (darar) and ensuring full compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the harmful act
Recognize that digging a second well which causes damage to an existing well is a harmful act (darar).
2
Understand the two opinions
First opinion: only filling the well is required. Second opinion (preferred): filling plus compensation for loss in value.
The first opinion considers filling sufficient to remove harm; the second adds financial compensation.
3
Identify the preferred opinion
The author states the second saying is sahih (correct) and attributes it to Imam al-Khassaf.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Learn the method of assessing loss
Compare the market value of the first well before and after the damage; the difference is the compensation.
Example: value drops from 50 to 40 rupees, so 10 rupees compensation.
5
Recognize analogous cases
The analogy of throwing garbage and demolishing a wall reinforces that the transgressor must undo harm and pay for losses.
These analogies are used in the text to support the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب احياء الموات اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ اس کو مکلفت کرے کہ اپنے کنویں کو بند کرے اور اسی مٹی سے بھر دے کیونکہ جو جرم کیا ہے اس کی تلافی کا یہ عمدہ طریقہ ہے اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے کہ کسی نے دوسرے کے گھر میں کوڑا کرکٹ پھینک دیا تو پھینکنے والے کو مکلف کیا جاتا ہے کہ اس کو اٹھائے -۲- اول کے کنویں کو جو نقصان پہنچا ہو وہ دوسرے سے لے لے پھر اس کے کنویں کو خود پاٹ دے اور نقصان کے پہچانے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دیکھے پہلے کنویں کی کیا قیمت ہے مثلاً پہلے پچاس روپے قیمت تھی اور دوسرے کنویں کی وجہ سے چالیس رہ گئی تو اس سے دس رو پینے جضمان لے لے اور کنواں خود پاٹ دے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے کسی کی دیوار گرادی تو اس سے ضمان لیا جائے گا پھر مالک اپنی دیوار خود درست کرائے گا۔ حضرت مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرا قول صحیح ہے اور امام خصاف نے اس کو اپنی کتاب ادب القاضی میں بیان کیا ہے اور نقصان کی معرفت کا مذکورہ طریقہ بھی انہوں نے بیان کیا ہے۔
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 14. He should be compelled to close his well and fill it with the same soil, because this is the excellent way to compensate for the crime committed. And this is exactly like someone throwing garbage into another's house; the thrower is compelled to remove it. (2) As for the loss that occurred to the first well, he should take (compensation) from the second (digger), then he himself should fill his well. And the way to know the loss is to see what was the value of the first well; for example, initially its value was fifty rupees, and due to the second well it became forty, so he should take ten rupees as compensation from him and fill the well himself. And this is like someone demolishing another's wall; compensation will be taken from him, then the owner will repair his own wall. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: The second saying is correct, and Imam al-Khassaf has mentioned it in his book Adab al-Qadi, and he has also mentioned the aforementioned method of knowing the loss.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a case where a person digs a second well that damages or drains the water of a pre-existing well. The text presents two opinions. The first opinion is that the second well digger must simply fill his well, and no further compensation is required. The second opinion, which the author (al-Marghinani) considers correct (sahih) and attributes to Imam al-Khassaf, is that the second well digger must (1) fill his own well, and (2) compensate for the decrease in the value of the first well. The method of assessing damage is by comparing the market value of the first well before and after the damage. The text illustrates with an example: if the first well was worth 50 rupees and after the second well it became worth 40, the second digger pays 10 rupees. This compensation is analogous to the case of someone demolishing another's wall: he pays the damage, but the owner rebuilds the wall. The analogies of throwing garbage and demolishing a wall reinforce that the transgressor must undo his harm and pay for losses. This ruling is from the chapter on Ihya al-Mawat, and it demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the one who causes damage must restore the status quo and compensate for any reduction in value.

The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the second opinion that includes compensation for loss in value, as preferred by the author. Although there is no explicit textual proof cited, the ruling is based on the principle of removing harm (darar) and compensation for damages, which is a well-established maxim in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ضمان (dhaman): Compensation or liability for damages caused to another's property.
نقصان (nuqsān): Decrease in value or loss incurred.
حافر (hāfir): The person who digs a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only fill his own well with soil.
B) Pay the full value of the first well.
C) Fill his well and pay for the decrease in the value of the first well.
D) Do nothing, as water loss is not compensable.

Key Takeaway
When a second well damages an existing well, the digger must fill his well and compensate for the loss in value, per the preferred Hanafi opinion.
