No Liability for the First Well Digger: The Concept of Tahjir in Hanafi Liability
Ruling that the first well digger is not liable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the first well digger is not liable for accidental deaths and distinguish Abu Hanifa's position from the Sahibayn's.

Core Idea
No liability without transgression — the first well digger's act is tahjir, a lawful act, even without the Imam's permission.

This passage addresses a scenario where a person digs a well in dead land (ihya al-mawat) as the first to revive it. If someone accidentally falls into the well and dies, is the digger liable? The Hanafi school unanimously says no, but the reasoning differs between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples. Understanding this difference illuminates the key Hanafi principle that liability (damān) is tied to transgression (ta'addī), and the concept of tahjir (enclosure) as a lawful act even without ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
What is the act and the harm? A person digs a well in dead land (mawat) as the first to revive it. Another person falls in and dies.
The well is the 'first well' (الاولى) dug in that land.
2
State the unanimous ruling
There is no liability (damān) on the digger, regardless of whether he had the Imam's permission.
The text states: 'لا ضمان فيه' – no liability.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
He considers digging to be tahjir (enclosure), which is permissible even without the Imam's permission. Since the act is permissible, there is no transgression (ta'addī), hence no liability.
Tahjir is a recognized legal act in Hanafi law for marking land for revival.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's position
They also rule no liability, but their specific reasoning is not detailed. The text implies they might consider the act transgressive but still exempt due to other factors.
The text says: 'وكذا ان كان بغير اذنه عندهما' – likewise without permission according to them.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome is the same (no liability), but the legal basis differs. This could affect other rulings, e.g., liability for later wells or for property damage.
The difference in reasoning may become significant in analogous cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پہلے کنویں میں کوئی گر کر مر جائے تو حافر پر ضمان نہیں وما عطب في الأولى فلا ضمان فيه لانه غير متعد ان كان باذن الامام فظاهر وكذا ان كان بغير اذنه عندهما والعذر لابي حنيفة انه يجعل الحفر تحجيرا وهو بسبيل منه بغير اذن الامام وان كان لا يملكه بدونه ترجمہ اور اول میں جو چیز ہلاک ہوگئی تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ غیر متعدی ہے ( زیادتی کرنے والا نہیں ہے ) اگر امام کی اجازت سے ہو تو ظاہر ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ اذن امام کے بغیر ہو صاحبین کے نزدیک۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کی جانب سے عذر یہ ہے کہ وہ کھودنے کو نجیر قرار دیتے ہیں اور وہ بغیر اذن امام کے تجیر کے حق پر ہے ( یعنی تجیر جائز ہے ) اگر چہ وہ اذن امام کے بغیر اس کا مالک نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح چونکہ پہلا شخص کنواں کھودنے میں حق بجانب ہے تو اگر اس میں کوئی گر کر مر جائے تو اس پر کوئی منمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں حاضر کا کوئی قصور نہیں ہے جیسے کوئی اپی مملوکہ زمین میں کنواں کھودے اور اس میں کوئی گر کر مر جائے تو اس پر کوئی ضمان نہیں عدم تعدی کی وجہ سے گنواں امام کی اجازت سے کھو دے یا بغیر اجازت کے اول میں تو کوئی اشکال ہی نہیں البتہ دوسری صورت میں امام صاحب کے مذہب کے مطابق اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے کہ اذن امام کے بغیر حافر اس کا مالک نہیں ہوتا تو تعدی ہوئی لہذ اضمان واجیب ہونا چاہیے۔ وابوحنیفہ کی جانب سے یہ عذر پیش کیا گیا یعنی یہ توجیہ پیش کی گئی ہے کہ انہوں نے حفر کو جیر قرار دیا ہے اور تجیر اذن امام کے بغیر جائز ہے اگر چہ اذن امام کے بغیر ملکیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی لیکن مجیر میں عدم تعدی ضرور ثابت ہوگئی لہذ اضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
If someone falls and dies in the first well, there is no liability on the digger. Translation: And whatever is destroyed in the first (well), there is no liability for it because he is not a transgressor. If it was with the permission of the Imam, it is apparent, and likewise if it was without his permission according to the two (Sahibayn). And the excuse of Abu Hanifa is that he considers digging as tahjir (enclosure), and he is entitled to tahjir without the Imam's permission, even though he does not own it without it. Explanation: Since the first person is rightful in digging the well, if someone falls and dies in it, there is no liability on him because there is no fault on his part, just like if someone digs a well on his own owned land and someone falls and dies, there is no liability due to non-transgression. If the well is dug with the Imam's permission or without, in the first case there is no difficulty. However, in the second case, according to the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) madhhab, an objection arises: the digger without permission does not own it, so there is transgression, thus liability should be wajib. And on behalf of Abu Hanifa, this excuse is presented: he has deemed digging as tahjir, and tahjir is permissible without the Imam's permission, even though ownership is not established, but non-transgression is certainly established, so liability is not wajib.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage deals with the liability for accidental deaths in a well dug by the first person who revives dead land. The ruling is unanimous: the digger is not liable for any death that occurs in the well. However, the reasoning differs between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). When the well is dug with the Imam's permission, all agree there is no liability because it is a lawful act. When dug without permission, the Sahibayn also rule no liability (though their specific reasoning is not elaborated here). The main focus is on Abu Hanifa's reasoning: he considers the act of digging as tahjir (marking/enclosure of land), which is permissible even without the Imam's permission, even though it does not confer full ownership. Since tahjir is a lawful act, there is no transgression (ta'addi), and therefore no liability. This distinguishes the case from a well dug wrongfully on another's property (which incurs liability). The lesson underscores the Hanafi principle that liability arises from transgression, and the first well digger, even without official permission, is engaged in a legally recognized activity (tahjir), thus not a transgressor. The quoted analogy of digging on one's own land reinforces that the absence of transgression negates liability.

Key Terms
تحجير (taḥjīr): Enclosure or marking of land to indicate intent to revive dead land; a preliminary act before actual revival.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or compensation; here specifically for death.
متعدی (mutaʿaddī): Transgressive; one who acts beyond his legal right, causing harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the digger of the first well not liable for a death even when he dug without the Imam's permission?
A) Because the digger owns the land even without permission.
B) Because digging is considered tahjir, which is permissible without permission.
C) Because the Imam is responsible for all accidents.
D) Because the death is considered an act of God.

Key Takeaway
The first digger of a well in dead land is never liable for accidental deaths because his act is considered lawful tahjir, not transgression.

Liability for Death in a Well Dug on Another's Property
Ruling statement on liability for death in a well dug without right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the digger of a well on another's property is liable for deaths and identify the condition of transgression that triggers liability.

Core Idea
Digging a well on another's property without right makes you liable for any death or damage.

This lesson examines a specific case from the Hidayah: a well dug on someone else's land without permission. The Hanafi school holds that the digger is liable because he has transgressed (ta'addi). This ruling contrasts with the first well, where the digger had a right to dig and is not liable. Understanding the role of transgression is key to applying the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is digging a well on another's property. The ruling is that the digger is liable (daman) for any death or damage in that well.
2
Locate the condition of liability
The condition is transgression (ta'addi): the digger acted without ownership or permission.
The text explicitly states 'because he is transgressive'.
3
Contrast with the first well
The first well (dug rightfully) does not incur liability because no transgression exists.
This contrast is implied in the source's reference to 'the second well'.
4
Apply the principle
If death or damage occurs in the second well, the digger must compensate, as liability follows transgression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے کنویں میں گر کر مر گیا تو مالک کنواں پر ضمان ہے وما عطب في الثانية ففيه الضمان لانه متعد فيه حيث حفر فی ملک غی اور جو چیز دوسرے میں بلاک ہوئی تو اس میں ضمان ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ اس نے اپنے ترجمه غیر کی ملک میں کنواں کھودا ہے۔ تشریح: اگر کوئی دوسرے کنویں میں گر کر مر جائے تو اس پر منمان ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی تعدی اور زیادتی ظاہر ہے کہ اس نے دوسرے کی ملک میں کنواں کھودا ہے۔
If someone falls and dies in the second well, then there is liability on the owner of the well. And whatever is destroyed in the second (well), there is liability in it because he is transgressive in it, since he dug in the property of another. Translation: And whatever perishes in the second, there is liability in it because he is transgressive in it, in the sense that he dug a well in another's property. Explanation: If someone falls and dies in the second well, then there will be liability because his transgression and excess are apparent: he dug a well in another's property.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This brief ruling establishes the contrast with the first well. If a person digs a well on someone else's property without right (as in the case of the 'second well' which is dug on the first person's land or within its rights), then any death or damage occurring in that well incurs liability (dhaman) on the digger. The reason is that the digger has transgressed (ta'addi) by encroaching on another's property. The ruling is straightforward: the presence of transgression makes the digger responsible for all consequences. This is a clear application of the Hanafi principle that liability follows transgression. The second well here is the one digging on the first well's land, so the digger is a usurper (ghasib) or similar, thus strictly liable.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for deaths or damages caused by transgression.
متعدی (mutaʿaddī): Transgressive; acting without right on another's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the digger of the second well liable for a death in that well?
A) Because the well is deeper than the first.
B) Because he dug in his own property.
C) Because he dug in another's property without right, making him a transgressor.
D) Because the Imam gave him permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that liability for death in a well follows transgression: if you dig without right on another's property, you are liable.

No Liability When Second Well is Outside the Harim
Ruling on no liability when second well is outside the harim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a second well is dug outside the harim of the first, and explain why there is no liability.

Core Idea
No liability without transgression: digging outside the harim is lawful use.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario where a second well is dug outside the harim (protected area) of an existing well, yet it causes the first well to dry up. The Hanafi school rules that the second digger is not liable for the water loss. On what basis? By understanding the concept of harim and the principle that liability only arises from transgression (ta'addi). Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is digging a second well outside the harim of the first, causing the first well's water to disappear. The ruling is no liability on the second digger.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the absence of transgression: the second digger dug outside the harim, so he is not muta'addi. The text also gives the analogy of a shopkeeper whose business suffers due to a new shop next door.
Rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the principle of ta'addi.
3
Understand the harim concept
The harim is 40 cubits around the well; within that zone, digging is prohibited without consent because it harms the first well. Outside, digging is lawful.
Harim is a protected area to prevent harm.
4
Apply the principle of ta'addi
Since no transgression occurred (the second well is outside the harim), there is no liability (dhaman). The second well also gets its own harim, except on the side facing the first well because of the first's prior right.
Liability requires transgression; lawful use of one's property is not actionable.
5
Note the broader implication
Underground water is not owned property; one cannot be forced to refrain from digging on his own land as long as no transgression occurs.
This aligns with the Hanafi position that harm from lawful acts does not create liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے شخص نے پہلے کنویں کے حریم کے باہر کنواں کھودا اور پہلے کنویں کا پانی ختم ہو گیا تو دوسرے پر کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے وان حفر الثانى بيرا وراء حريم الأولى فذهب ماء البير الاولى لاشيء عليه لانه غير متعد في حفرها وللثاني الحريم من الجوانب الثلاثة دون الجانب الاول لسبق ملك الحافر الاول فيه ترجمہ اور اگر دوسرے نے کنواں کھودا پہلے کے حریم سے باہر پس پہلے کنویں کا پانی ختم ہو گیا تو اس پر (ثانی پر ) کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے کھودنے میں متعدی نہیں ہے اور دوسرے کو تین طرف سے حریم ملے گا نہ کہ پہلے کی جانب میں حافر اول کی ملکیت کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے اس میں۔ تشریح دوسرے نے پہلے کنویں کے حریم سے باہر یعنی چالیس ذراع ہٹ کر کنواں کھودا جس کی وجہ سے پہلے کنویں کا پانی ختم ہو گیا تو دوسرے پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں پائی گئی کیونکہ اس نے اول کے حریم سے باہر کنواں کھودا ہے پھر دوسرے کنویں کو بھی حریم چاہیے تو فرمایا کہ پہلے کنویں کی جانب میں تو پہلے کنویں کا حریم ہے چالیس ذراع تک اس میں تو دوسرے کو حریم نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ اس سمت پہلے کی ملک مقدم ہے البتہ اس جانب کے علاوہ باقی تینوں جانبوں میں دوسرے کو حریم ملے گا۔ تنبیہ پانی زمین کے نیچے کسی کی ملکیت نہیں ہے تو اس پر یہ جبر نہیں ہو سکتا کہ یہاں سے اپنا کنواں بنانے جبکہ اس نے کوئی تعدی نہیں کی اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی کی دکان ہے۔ اور اس چیز کی دکان دوسرے نے اس کے برابر میں کرلی جس سے پہلی دکان ٹھپ ہوگئی تو دوسرے پر کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۳۵ ج ۲
If the second person dug a well outside the harim of the first, and the water of the first well disappeared, there is no liability on him. And if the second dug a well beyond the harim of the first, and the water of the first well went away, nothing is upon him because he is not transgressive in its digging. And the second gets the harim from three sides, not from the first side due to the precedence of the ownership of the first digger therein. Translation: And if the second dug a well beyond the harim of the first, so the water of the first well disappeared, then there is no liability on him (the second) because he is not transgressive in its digging. And the second will get harim from three sides, not from the side of the first due to the precedence of ownership of the first digger in it. Explanation: The second dug a well outside the harim of the first, i.e., forty cubits away, causing the water of the first well to disappear, so there will be no liability on the second because no transgression occurred since he dug outside the harim of the first. Then the second well also requires a harim, so it is said: on the side of the first well, the first well has its harim up to forty cubits, so the second will not get harim in that direction because the ownership of the first is prior; however, on the remaining three sides, the second will get harim. Note: Water underground is not owned by anyone, so he cannot be forced not to dig his well when he has not committed transgression. And this is like someone's shop: another person opened a shop next to it, causing the first shop to become idle, so there is no liability on the second. (Majma' al-Anhar, p. 535, vol. 2)
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a second well is dug outside the harim (protected area) of the first well, yet it causes the first well's water to dry up. The ruling is that the second digger is not liable for this loss. The reason is that he dug beyond the harim, so he is not a transgressor (ghayr muta'addi). The harim of a well is forty cubits (dhira') on all sides, which is a protected zone where no one else can dig without potentially causing harm to the first well. Since the second well is outside that zone, the second digger is within his rights. The text also explains that the second well itself is entitled to a harim, but only on three sides; on the side facing the first well, the first well's prior right prevents the second from claiming a harim there. A تنبیہ (note) adds that underground water is not owned property; thus, one cannot be forced to refrain from digging on his own land as long as no transgression occurs. The analogy of a shopkeeper whose business suffers due to a new shop next door illustrates that losses from lawful competition are not compensable. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that liability only arises from transgression (ta'addi), not from lawful use of one's own property even if it inadvertently harms another.

Key Terms
حریم (ḥarīm): The protected area around a well or water source, typically forty cubits, within which no one else may dig without causing harm.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for loss caused; here specifically for water loss.
تعدی (taʿaddī): Transgression; acting beyond one's right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the second well digger not liable if his well outside the harim causes the first well to dry up?
A) Because the first well was not properly constructed.
B) Because he is not a transgressor since he dug outside the harim.
C) Because water underground is owned by the state.
D) Because the first well owner should have dug deeper.

Key Takeaway
Liability for water loss requires transgression; digging outside the harim is lawful use, even if it causes harm.

The Harim of an Underground Channel (Qanat)
Ruling on the protected area (harim) for a qanat (underground channel)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the harim of a qanat and identify the mufta bihi according to the mashayikh.

Core Idea
A qanat's harim depends on whether water has surfaced: before surfacing, no fixed measure; after surfacing, 500 cubits.

The harim (protected area) around water sources varies by type. For an underground channel (qanat), the Hanafi imams differed. This lesson walks through the positions of Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and the Sahibayn, and the later preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and its practical importance
The issue is whether a qanat (underground irrigation channel) has a fixed harim, and if so, what its measure is. This determines where others may dig wells or build structures nearby.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: no harim until water surfaces, then 500 cubits. Imam Muhammad: 40 cubits (like a well). Sahibayn: reportedly agree with Muhammad.
3
Analyze the analogies (qiyas) used
Abu Hanifa analogizes the qanat before surfacing to an underground river (flexible), and after surfacing to a spring (500 cubits). Muhammad analogizes it to a well (fixed 40 cubits).
The illa for Muhammad is the similarity of a finite water source; for Abu Hanifa, it is the flowing nature.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The later authorities (mashayikh) preferred Abu Hanifa's view for the pre-surface stage (flexible) and adopted 500 cubits for post-surface, rejecting the 40-cubit fixed measure.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply to a real scenario
In Balochistan, where qanats are common, the harim before surfacing is whatever suffices for maintenance; after surfacing, it is 500 cubits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کاریز ( کھلی نہر ) کا حریم کتنی مقدار ہے والقناة لها حريم بقدر ما يصلحها وعن محمد انه بمنزلة البير فى استحقاق الحريم وقيل هو عندهما وعنده لا حريم لها مالم يظهر الماء على الارض لانه نهر فى التحقيق فيعتبر بالنهر الظاهر قالوا وعند ظهور الماء على الأرض هو بمنزلة عين فوارة فيقدر حريمه بخمس مائة ذراع ترجمہ اور کاریز اس کا تریم اتنا ہو گا جو اس کے لئے مناسب ہو اور محمدؐ سے منقول ہے کہ یہ استحقاق حریم کے سلسلہ میں کنویں کے مثل ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مناسبین کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کے لئے حریم نہیں جب تک کہ پانی زمین پر ظاہر نہ ہو اس لئے یہ حقیقت میں نہر ہے تو اس کو کھلی نہر قیاس کیا جائے گا مشائخ نے فرمایا اور پانی کے ظاہر ہونے کے وقت زمین پر وہ جوشندہ چشمہ کے مثل ہے تو اس کا حریم پانچ سو ذراع کیساتھ مقدر ہوگا۔ تشریح ایک تو کھلی ہوئی نہر ہوتی ہے اور کبھی نہ ایسی ہوتی ہے جس کو اوپر سے پاٹ دیا جاتا ہے اس کو قاہ اور کاریز کہتے ہیں نیز پٹی ہوئی چھوٹی بند نالی کو بھی قنات اور کاریز کہتے ہیں اور بلوچستان میں تو آبپاشی کا یہی طریقہ ہے۔
What is the measure of the harim of a qanat (covered channel)? And the qanat has a harim to the extent that suffices for its repair. And from Muhammad, it is said that it is like a well in entitlement to harim. And it is said that according to the two (Sahibayn) it is like that, but according to him (Abu Hanifa), there is no harim for it as long as water does not appear on the surface, because it is in reality a river, so it is analogized to an apparent river. The mashayikh said: and when water appears on the surface, it is like a gushing spring, so its harim is estimated at five hundred cubits. Explanation: There are two types: one is an open canal, and sometimes there is one that is covered from above, which is called qanat and kariz. Also, a small covered channel is called qanat and kariz. In Balochistan, this is the method of irrigation.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage discusses the harim (protected area) for a qanat, which is an underground water channel (also known as kariz). The Hanafi school has multiple positions. According to a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the qanat's harim is like that of a well, meaning forty cubits on each side. However, the more established position (especially of Abu Hanifa) is that as long as the water has not reached the surface (i.e., the qanat is entirely underground), it has no specific harim because it is analogous to an underground river (nahr batini) that is not subject to the same fixed boundaries. Instead, its harim is whatever is needed for its maintenance and repair. Once the water emerges on the surface, it becomes like a spring ('ayn fawwara), and then its harim is fixed at five hundred cubits (dira'). The passage attributes this view to the mashayikh (later authorities). The term 'qanat' is distinguished from an open canal (nahr zahir); an open canal's harim is governed by separate rules. The lesson highlights the flexibility in Hanafi law regarding different types of water sources: the harim varies based on the nature of the source.

Key Terms
قنات (qanāt): An underground channel for irrigation, also called kariz.
حریم (ḥarīm): Protected zone around a water source to prevent damage.
نهر ظاهر (nahr ẓāhir): An open, visible river or canal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mashayikh, what is the harim of a qanat after its water appears on the surface?
A) 40 cubits, like a well.
B) 500 cubits, like a spring.
C) No harim at all.
D) Whatever the owner decides.

Key Takeaway
The harim of a qanat is not fixed until water surfaces; thereafter it is 500 cubits.

beginner

The Harim of a Tree Planted in Dead Land
Ruling with proof: harim of tree in mawat land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the harim for a tree planted in mawat land, identify its measure (five cubits) based on a hadith, and apply it to prevent encroachment.

Core Idea
A tree planted in dead land owns a five-cubit harim on each side — no one else may plant there.

When you plant a tree on unowned dead land, you gain a right to a surrounding zone called the harim. This passage teaches us the exact measure of that zone and why it exists, based on a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud. Understanding this helps protect your rights as a land improver.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The passage states that a tree planted in mawat (dead, unowned) land has a harim. The ruling is that no other person may plant a tree within this harim.
The harim is a protective zone; it is not ownership of the land itself but a right of use.
2
Determine the measure of the harim
The passage explicitly states the measure: five cubits (dhira) from each side of the tree.
One cubit is approximately the length from elbow to fingertips; about 46-50 cm.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is a hadith (reported in Sunan Abi Dawud) that specifies this measure. The commentator mentions that the hadith is the basis.
The hadith is considered ahad (single-transmitter), but it is accepted as a binding proof in this context.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The harim is necessary because the planter needs space to stand, pick fruit, store it, and sometimes dry it. The measure of five cubits is deemed sufficient for these needs.
This illustrates how fiqh considers practical human needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ارض موات میں لگائے جانے والے درخت کا بھی حریم ہے
والشجرة تغرس في ارض موات لها حريم ايضا حتى لم يكن لغيره ان يغرس شجرا في حريمها لانه يحتاج الى حريم له فيه ثمره ويضعه فيه وهو مقدر بخمسة اذرع من كل جانب به ورد الحديث
ترجمہ: اور درخت جو لگایا جائے افتادہ زمین میں اس کے لئے بھی حریم ہے یہاں تک کہ دوسرے کو حق نہ ہوگا کہ اس کے حریم میں درخت لگائے کہ درخت لگانے والا اس کے حریم کا محتاج ہے جس میں وہ پھل توڑے اور رکھے اور وہ جانب سے پانچ ذراع کے ساتھ مقدر ہے اس کے ساتھ حدیث وارد ہوئی ہے۔
تشریح: جس نے افتادہ زمین میں درخت لگایا تو درخت کا بھی حریم ہوگا جس کی مقدار پانچ ذراع ہے جو حدیث سے ثابت ہے جو ث ابوداؤد میں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو ضرورت ہوگی اس جگہ کی جس میں کھڑا ہو کر وہ پھل توڑے اور اس جگہ میں رکھے اور کبھی سکھانے کی بھی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے۔
The tree planted in dead land also has a harim, so that it is not permissible for another to plant a tree in its harim, because he needs a harim in which to pick its fruit and place it, and it is measured as five cubits from each side; a hadith is reported about this. Translation: And the tree planted in dead land also has a harim, to the extent that another has no right to plant a tree in its harim, because the planter needs its harim to pick fruit and place it, and it is measured as five cubits from each side; a hadith is reported about this. Commentary: Whoever plants a tree in dead land, the tree also has a harim, the quantity of which is five cubits, proven by the hadith reported in Sunan Abi Dawud. Because he will need a place to stand and pick fruit, and a place to put it, and sometimes he needs a place to dry it.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the harim (protective zone) of a tree planted in mawat (dead/unowned) land. The matn states the ruling that a tree has a harim of five cubits on each side, and that no one else may plant in that harim. The proof is a hadith (from Sunan Abi Dawud). The commentator explains the reasoning: the planter needs space to stand, pick fruit, store it, and sometimes dry it. The harim is quantified by the hadith itself. This is a clear example of a ruling established by a specific textual evidence (dalil naqli).

Key Terms
حریم (harim): A protective zone around a tree or water source that belongs to the owner of the tree/water and cannot be used by others.
موات (mawat): Dead, unowned land that has not been cultivated or owned by anyone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the measure of the harim of a tree planted in mawat land according to the hadith?
A) 5 cubits
B) 10 cubits
C) 500 cubits
D) Depends on the tree size

Key Takeaway
A tree planted in mawat land has a fixed harim of five cubits on each side, derived from a specific hadith, and no one may plant within that zone.
